< Text>
I was in Santa Cruz about 2 months ago on a business trip and I stayed at the Hotel Paradox. I asked if they could recommend a place nearby where I could get a bite to eat and have a beer or two and they recommended  Beach Hut Deli which is located a block's walk from the hotel.
Being that I was in Santa Cruz I decided to get the signature sandwich The Santa Cruz and it was amazing. I also was able to try a couple of local Santa Cruz beers and they were great as well.
Needless to say the sandwich and beers I had were great but what is also worth mentioning is the staff and their customers are very friendly too. I sat at the bar in between a fisherman and a Silicon Valley lawyer and they welcomed me right into the conversation they were having and I felt like I knew both for many years.
Thank you Beach Hut Deli and Santa Cruz for making a guy from out of town feel welcomed. I'll certainly see you all again when I'm back in town in July.< /Text>

<user_id>109768486251334983010< /user_id><Name>Bridget Penn< /Name>< Date>
1559839029639</Date>
<Rating>4< /Rating>< Review>
We've always picked Claremont Village for classier nights out, and Downtown Pomona where most of the divier bars and dance clubs are, if we want to get DOWN. Although I do enjoy a good ratchet nightlife experience once in a while, Acerogami is the nicest bar in the downtown area and worthy of taking guests to. I've actually never been to the Glass House, but I love going to this attached bar. It's a pretty, very spacious layout with perfect lighting, a minimalist and nice ambiance without being too fancy. The bartenders are nice and laid-back. The drink prices are amazing and far from Claremont drink prices, too! A must-visit if you are planning a night out in the area< /Review>

<review>Love, love, love this nursery! They have a great selection of plants, even some semi-rare ones. They also have carnivorous plants beyond your basic venus fly trap and lots of air plants. The plants are really well taken care of and fairly priced. I have seen other nurseries charge more for the same type of plants in just OK condition. And their pot options! I bought a couple of terracotta pots that were made by a local artist here.

I do like that the nursery don't have much of a huge social media presence, it makes it that more special when you do find one of the plants on your list :) And what's the worst case if you don't? You'll probably still leave with a plant, or two, or three, and have spent some time in a serene space. Great staff, too, keep up the good work!< /review></record>

</record></dataset><record>
< review>
The absolutely best dog park as far as landscaping goes is located in Vallejo!
Better than any other dog parks within an hour or twos drive.
Wardlaw is just a gorgeous park. I almost always end up chit chatting or in conversation with other friendly dog owners. It's not snooty as far as I can tell, people often clean more than their share, no one has gotten upset at barking dog's.
It's a very nice place to spend a few minutes or a few hours with your four legged bark buddies.
Bring your own sanitizer spray. Bags are biodegradable but dificult to open, one kind lady taught me to rip open a small tear at the top to find/create a separation point.
Lots of regulars seem well aquatinted with each other and even if they don't know the humans names, they'll know each other's dogs names.
It's ideal for me as I cannot walk them due to physical limitations.
I can make it walking from one chair location to another and thereby get in a little extra exercise myself. If you don't have painful limitations that doesn't seem like a big deal but it is a great set up for me and a perfect match for my needs. I'll get some better photos, these are only by the very front in the small side. It isn't an accurate representation on how nice it is.</review>

<resp>None</resp><Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
I have been to a LOT of dog parks, and this is one of the nicest I've seen. I stop whenever I'm in the area, and it's always in excellent condition. The surface is grass. The large dog park is built on a gentle slope, which I think helps it drain so the turf doesn't get muddy and torn up from rain. (And then patchy and dusty in summer.) The slope and irregular shape make it more interesting than the typical flat rectangle, and there's a path around the perimeter. The people and dogs I've met have all been friendly. Plenty of parking, double gate, small & large dog sections, water, poop bags, and good fencing. Just a pleasant place for your dog and you.<//text>
